  :                            62 
  :                            63 LIBRARY	$equ	LIBRARY_XDR
  :                            64 
  :                            65 .	this library is for a stream continuum
  :                            66 .	so nothing is set up to initialise
  :                            67 .	a field pointer of any kind
  :                            68 .	except it is a counted stream and must
  :                            69 .	do nothing if no bytes are available
  :                            70 .	and stop when it runs out of bytes
  :                            71 
  :                            72 .	this generation runs with the defaults
  :                            73 .	ASCII / UTF8, 8-bit byte
  :                            74 
  :                            75 .	the initialisation call READ_START
  :                            76 .	programs the staging registers
  :                            77 .	RDATAC+RDATA+Q to shift two bytes
  :                            78 .	per word from network buffers,
  :                            79 .	which store datalike this:
  :                            80 .	
  :                            81 .		_________________________________
  :                            82 .		| 0000 0000 XXXX xxxx XXXX xxxx |
  :                            83 .		|_______________________________|
  :                            84 
  :                            85 .	immediately on acquisition via register *q++
  :                            86 .	if bstream16r is on, RDATAC is decremented
  :                            87 .	from 24 to 16 and RDATA is shifted 8 bits
  :                            88 .	left:
  :                            89 
  :                            90 .		_________________________________
  :                            91 .		| XXXX xxxx XXXX xxxx 0000 0000 |
  :                            92 .		|_______________________________|
  :                            93 
  :                            94 
  :                            95 .	in contrast to 8 bit data in program data
  :                            96 .	which uses all 24 bits in the data word:
  :                            97 
  :                            98 .		_________________________________
  :                            99 .		| XXXX xxxx XXXX xxxx XXXX xxxx |
  :                            100 .		|_______________________________|
  :                            101 
  :                            102 .	the staging registers deliver or output
  :                            103 .	16 bits per word if PSR flags
  :                            104 
  :                            105 .		b$stream16r
  :                            106 .		b$stream16w
  :                            107 
  :                            108 .	are on, otherwise 24 bits per word
  :                            109 
  :                            110 
  :                            111 	$list	2
  :                            112 
  :                            113 .	binary and math library data character code transparent
  :                            114

  :                            40 
  :                            41 
  :                            42 .	these are used in conjunction with
  :                            43 .	hard TCP / RPC / XDR / which handle
  :                            44 .	segments fragmented over IP plus messages
  :                            45 .	fragmented over segments with record
  :                            46 .	marks
  :                            47 
  :                            48 .	external data is 24-bit in application
  :                            49 .	space typically in scratch registers or
  :                            50 .	internal stack

  :                            53 ieee754_64_2f
00:006040 3D0000              +54 	fret	0
  :                            55 f2_ieee754_64
00:006041 3D0000              +56 	fret	0
  :                            57 
  :                            58 .	below this line routines are available
  :                            59 .	for very simple UDP socket user programs
  :                            60 .	which access the 16-bit data in socket
  :                            61 .	buffers
  :                            62 
  :                            63 .	user datagrams have to be very short or DNF
  :                            64 .	so that no-fragments is assured for these
  :                            65 .	routines to be used safely

  :                            41 .	if the acquired mantissa fits in 72 bits use this conversion
  :                            42 .	because this should be integer accurate if it is correct code
  :                            43 
  :                            44 .	the technique of adding together two overlapping numbers
  :                            45 .	forces a small inaccuracy through hardware rounding. That
  :                            46 .	can't be accepted if the mantissa was 100% representable
  :                            47 .	in the first place

00:0060B5 E70009              +57 	dlsc	TRIPLE		. otherwise look for a sign change
00:0060B6 450019              +58 	lr, xi	25		. from sign zero
00:0060B7 500006              +59 	lx	6
00:0060B8 F600BF              +60 	jxge	around		. bit 47 is also zero
00:0060B9 200009              +61 	sa	TRIPLE

00:0060BC C7000A              +64 	ds	TRIPLE+1	. into the LS 48 bits

00:0060C4 B00011              +74 	xor	SIGNS		. now switch to working in signed
00:0060C5 200008              +75 	sa	QUAD

  :                            5: 	$include	recipro1.msm
  :                            1 
  :                            2 .	192-bit floating reciprocal routine
  :                            3 
  :                            4 .	very long and plodding, but has at least established
  :                            5 .	the mantissa can successfully be reciprocated
  :                            6 .	in a separate step from reciprocating the exponent
  :                            7 .	which is a fortunate discovery for writing 
  :                            8 .	any smarter reciprocal routine
  :                            9         
  :                            10 .	used for dividing 192 bits by 192 bits
  :                            11 .	multiply by 192-bit reciprocal of the divisor 
  :                            12 .	is done instead
  :                            13 
  :                            14
